<doc id="26011102" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26011102" title="Madame Aphrodite (musical)">
In mid-December, it was announced that the premiere of "Madame Aphrodite" had been postponed yet again, albeit this time by only two days. True to form, the show opened on Friday, December 29, 1961, at 7:30pm. The reviews were mixed to negative, with Mosel's book repeatedly identified as the biggest problem. Jack Gaver stated that "the libretto is not a good one. The story seemed to border almost on fantasy, yet never quite takes a step over that line. Might have been better if it had". Writing in the "New York Times", Lewis Funke commented that "the story is lumbering and humourless, with much of what is passed off as comedy being <a href="malapropism">malapropisms</a> uttered by the fake beautician". He was referring to Madame Aphrodite's habit of substituting words of similar sound but different meaning: examples cited by Funke included "migratin' headache" (for "<a href="migraine">migraine</a> headache") and "incinerating" for "insinuating". The comic device was also reflected in at least one song, "Sales Reproach" (i.e. "Sales Approach"). Most of the show's critics, however, found this irritating rather than endearing.

<doc id="26012433" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26012433" title="Winter's Bone">
A few nights later, the same three Milton women who beat Ree come to her house. They offer to take her to "[her] daddy's bones." The women place a burlap sack on her head and drive her to a pond, where they get into a rowboat and row to the shallow area where her father's submerged body lies. They tell Ree to reach into the freezing water and grasp her father's hands so they can cut them off with a chainsaw; the severed, decaying arms will serve as proof of death for the authorities. Ree takes the hands to the sheriff, telling him that someone flung them onto the porch of her house.

<doc id="26012749" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26012749" title="The Baby Show">
<a href="Cerie%20Xerox">Cerie Xerox</a> (<a href="Katrina%20Bowden">Katrina Bowden</a>) announces her engagement during a gathering for <a href="Jenna%20Maroney">Jenna Maroney</a>'s (<a href="Jane%20Krakowski">Jane Krakowski</a>) birthday, and says that she wants to be a "young hot mom". <a href="Liz%20Lemon">Liz Lemon</a> (<a href="Tina%20Fey">Tina Fey</a>) confronts her own marital and maternal status. She speaks with Jenna about this, and Jenna proceeds to tell all of the men in the office—<a href="Frank%20Rossitano">Frank Rossitano</a> (<a href="Judah%20Friedlander">Judah Friedlander</a>), <a href="Toofer%20Spurlock">James "Toofer" Spurlock</a> (<a href="Keith%20Powell">Keith Powell</a>), and <a href="J.%20D.%20Lutz">J. D. Lutz</a> (John Lutz)—that Liz is looking for someone to get her pregnant. Later that day, Liz sees Cerie in the makeup department getting herself made up. Anna (<a href="Bridget%20Moloney">Bridget Moloney</a>), the makeup artist has her baby at work with her. She asks Liz to hold the baby for a while, so Liz takes the baby for a stroll around the 30 Rock building. Suddenly she realizes that she is no longer in the building, but is now in her apartment. She hurries back to the office with the baby, and <a href="Pete%20Hornberger">Pete Hornberger</a> (<a href="Scott%20Adsit">Scott Adsit</a>) fixes the situation.

<doc id="26013114" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26013114" title="Sharon Burley">
Sharon Burley
Sharon Kay Burley Sullivan (born 8 May 1956 in <a href="Tripoli">Tripoli</a>, <a href="Libya">Libya</a>) is an <a href="Australia">Australian</a> <a href="figure%20skater">figure skater</a> who competed in ladies singles. She finished first at the <a href="Australian%20Figure%20Skating%20Championships">Australian Figure Skating Championships</a> four times and competed at the <a href="1976%20Winter%20Olympic%20Games">1976 Winter Olympic Games</a>, coming in twentieth.
Burley is the daughter of Olympic figure skater <a href="Nancy%20Burley">Nancy Burley</a> and the sister of Australian champion <a href="Robyn%20Burley">Robyn Burley</a>.

<doc id="26016245" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26016245" title="Nellie Morse Stakes">
The Nellie Morse Stakes is an <a href="United%20States">American</a> <a href="Thoroughbred">Thoroughbred</a> <a href="horse%20race">horse race</a> held annually in January at <a href="Laurel%20Park%20Racecourse">Laurel Park Racecourse</a> in <a href="Laurel%2C%20Maryland">Laurel, Maryland</a>. The Nellie Morse Stakes, is open to fillies and mares age four years old and up and is run at one mile (eight furlongs) on the dirt.

<doc id="26016378" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26016378" title="Anvil Point">
The point is within the grounds of <a href="Durlston%20Country%20Park">Durlston Country Park</a> and is on the hill about three kilometres from Swanage town centre. Anvil Point is in the eastern part of the <a href="Portland%20stone">Portland limestone</a> and the <a href="Purbeck%20Group">Purbeck beds</a> that stretches from <a href="Durlston%20Bay">Durlston Head</a> to <a href="St%20Alban%27s%20Head">St. Aldhelm's Head</a>. For a long time the cliffs along this stretch of coast were quarried at <a href="Tilly%20Whim%20Caves">Tilly Whim Caves</a>, <a href="Dancing%20Ledge">Dancing Ledge</a>, <a href="Seacombe%20Quarry">Seacombe</a> and <a href="Winspit">Winspit</a>. The cliffs are superb for geologists and also for walkers. They are very well known to rock climbers.

<doc id="26016523" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26016523" title="Washington Park Futurity Stakes">
The Washington Park Futurity Stakes was an American <a href="Thoroughbred%20horse%20race">Thoroughbred horse race</a> run annually at the now defunct <a href="Washington%20Park%20Race%20Track">Washington Park Race Track</a> in <a href="Woodlawn%2C%20Chicago">Woodlawn, Chicago</a>. A race on dirt for two-year-olds, it was first run in 1937 as a six furlong event. Placed on hiatus for two years, it returned as an annual feature in 1940.
From 1959 through 1961 the race was hosted by Chicago's <a href="Arlington%20Park">Arlington Park</a> race track where it was run at a distance of six and a half furlongs. Made permanent at Arlington Park, the Washington Park Futurity was merged with the <a href="Arlington%20Futurity%20Stakes">Arlington Futurity Stakes</a> and is known as the <a href="Arlington-Washington%20Futurity%20Stakes">Arlington-Washington Futurity Stakes</a>.
Speed record: (at distance of 6 furlongs)

<doc id="26017095" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26017095" title="J. David Spurlock">
J. David Spurlock
Jess David Spurlock (born November 18, 1959) is an author, illustrator, editor, and artist's-rights advocate best known as the founder of Vanguard Productions, a publisher of art books, graphic novels, and prints.
J. David Spurlock was born on November 18, 1959 in <a href="Memphis%2C%20Tennessee">Memphis, Tennessee</a>. He moved to <a href="Dallas%2C%20Texas">Dallas, Texas</a> in 1973. 
As a <a href="comic%20book">comic book</a> artist, he co-<a href="penciler">penciled</a> and <a href="inker">inked</a> the <a href="alternative%20press">alternative press</a> comic "Sparkplug" #1 (March 1993), from <a href="Heroic%20Publishing">Heroic Publishing</a>'s Hero Comics imprint, credited as David Spurlock. The following year he contributed a text page to a Dallas, Texas, tribute comic honoring industry legend <a href="Jack%20Kirby">Jack Kirby</a>, who had recently died.
Spurlock founded Vanguard Productions in 1993, although he had used that name, in conjunction with Sparrowlake Enterprises, to self-publish the <a href="comic%20book">comic book</a> "Badge" #1 in 1981. The company initially had been founded to publish a comics anthology, "Tales from the Edge", with 15 issues released as of 2010. The company then moved into art books, biographies and eventually <a href="graphic%20novel">graphic novels</a>, including <a href="Neal%20Adams">Neal Adams</a>' "Monsters" (2003), (originally serialized in the comics anthology series "Echoes of Future Past", published by Adams' <a href="Continuity%20Studios">Continuity Studios</a>), with four additional story pages plus additional Adams material. <a href="DC%20Comics">DC Comics</a> editor <a href="Julius%20Schwartz">Julius Schwartz</a>, an architect of the <a href="Silver%20Age%20of%20Comic%20Books">Silver Age of Comic Books</a>, said "Spurlock's line of books serve as the vanguard of Silver Age comics histories." Other comics magazines and collections published by Vanguard beginning in 2001 include "Space Cowboy", "<a href="Jesse%20James">Jesse James</a> Classic Western Collection", "<a href="Steve%20Ditko">Steve Ditko</a>: Space Wars" and <a href="Wally%20Wood">Wally Wood</a>'s "The Complete Lunar Tunes" and "The Wizard King".
In an article on the <a href="Fort%20Worth%2C%20Texas">Fort Worth, Texas</a>, comics artist <a href="Pat%20Boyette">Pat Boyette</a>, <a href="Don%20Mangus">Don Mangus</a>, who assisted Spurlock during this time, wrote of the early Vanguard comics that,
Spurlock co-created the <a href="Wally%20Wood">Wally Wood</a> Scholarship Fund with Wood's brother, Glenn Wood, for students of the <a href="School%20of%20Visual%20Arts">School of Visual Arts</a>. In a joint venture with <a href="Marvel%20Comics">Marvel Comics</a> and Diamond Comic Distributors, Vanguard Productions in 2002 sponsored artist <a href="Jim%20Steranko">Jim Steranko</a>'s "The Spirit of America" benefit print, created to fund an art scholarship "for victims of anti-American terrorism".
In 2008, Spurlock, with artist and publisher <a href="Neal%20Adams">Neal Adams</a> and the <a href="David%20S.%20Wyman%20Institute%20for%20Holocaust%20Studies">David S. Wyman Institute for Holocaust Studies</a> Arts & Letters Council, spearheaded a petition campaign in which over 450 comic book creators and cartoonists urged the <a href="Auschwitz-Birkenau%20State%20Museum">Auschwitz-Birkenau State Museum</a> to return to artist <a href="Dina%20Babbitt">Dina Babbitt</a> seven portraits she was forced to paint in the Auschwitz death camp in 1944.
Vanguard's "Wally's World: The Brilliant Life and Tragic Death of <a href="Wally%20Wood">Wally Wood</a>, the World's Second-Best Comic Book Artist" (2004), by Spurlock and Steve Sarger, was nominated for a 2007 Eisner Award for "Best Comics-Related Book".

This is a listing of the horses that finished in either first, second, or third place and the number of starters in the <a href="Nellie%20Morse%20Stakes">Nellie Morse Stakes</a> (1941-present), an American Thoroughbred Stakes race for fillies and mares four years-old and up at six furlongs run on dirt at <a href="Laurel%20Park%20Racecourse">Laurel Park Racecourse</a> in <a href="Laurel%2C%20Maryland">Laurel, Maryland</a>.

<doc id="26017802" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26017802" title="James W. Maney">
At age 17, Maney began working for the <a href="Union%20Pacific%20Railroad">Union Pacific Railroad</a>. By age 22 he had become a railroad contractor, which became his lifelong career. At the age of 22 he built three miles on the <a href="Burlington%20and%20Missouri%20River%20Railroad">Burlington and Missouri River Railroad</a> in the state of <a href="Nebraska">Nebraska</a>. His next contract was in <a href="South%20Dakota">South Dakota</a>. When <a href="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a> was opened for settlement in 1889, Maney built the second railroad into the state. Within months of the opening of the territory, he settled in the area which would become Oklahoma City. By 1900 he was reputed to be "the largest railroad contractor in Oklahoma."
<doc id="26017811" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26017811" title="Simone James">

<doc id="26017831" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26017831" title="Princess Bathildis of Schaumburg-Lippe">
<doc id="26017841" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26017841" title="Rosa (given name)">
<doc id="26017843" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26017843" title="List of birds of Yellowstone National Park">
Scolopacidae is a large diverse family of small to medium-sized shorebirds including the sandpipers, curlews, godwits, shanks, tattlers, woodcocks, snipes, dowitchers and phalaropes. The majority of these species eat small invertebrates picked out of the mud or soil. Different lengths of legs and bills enable multiple species to feed in the same habitat, particularly on the coast, without direct competition for food. There are 23 Yellowstone species.

<doc id="26017998" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26017998" title="M'pozo River">
<doc id="26018004" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26018004" title="CAL Actor Language">
<doc id="26018013" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26018013" title="Alaska Division of Homeland Security &amp; Emergency Management">
<doc id="26018014" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26018014" title="Vander Veer Park Historic District">
In 1885 the city of Davenport acquired the property that had been the Scott County Fairgrounds. It is a significant example of landscape planning, and of the civic improvements that were being made by the city in the late 19th and early 20th centuries. Five years after the land was purchased and improved it was named Central Park after <a href="New%20York%20City">New York City</a>'s park of the <a href="Central%20Park">same name</a>. Like its namesake it featured naturalistic landscaping, a <a href="Greenhouse">glasshouse</a>, floral gardens, a large pond, picnic pavilion and a picturesque bridge. Central Park was the first major park established by the City of Davenport. The year that it opened the city established the Board of Parks Commissioners. They acquired other properties and established residential parks similar to Central Park. The parks included both Lookout Park, later renamed <a href="Riverview%20Terrace%20Historic%20District">Riverview Terrace</a>, and <a href="Prospect%20Park%20Historic%20District%20%28Davenport%2C%20Iowa%29">Prospect Park</a> that were brought into the city's system in 1894. <a href="Fejervary%20Park">Fejervary Park</a> was acquired in 1902. Other major projects in the city's beautification program included riverfront improvement that created <a href="LeClaire%20Park">LeClaire Park</a> and included the <a href="W.D.%20Petersen%20Memorial%20Music%20Pavilion">W.D. Petersen Memorial Music Pavilion</a>, <a href="Dillon%20Memorial">Dillon Fountain</a>, and <a href="Union%20Station%20and%20Burlington%20Freight%20House">Union Station</a> between 1911 and 1931.

<doc id="26018911" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26018911" title="One Shot (JLS song)">
"One Shot" is a song by English <a href="boy%20band">boy band</a> <a href="JLS">JLS</a>. It was written by <a href="Soulshock%20%26amp%3B%20Karlin">Soulshock & Karlin</a>, Michael Warren, Brandon White, and Sean Hurley. It was released as their third and final single from their <a href="JLS%20%28album%29">self-titled debut album</a> on 21 February 2010. The song reached the A-List on <a href="BBC%20Radio%201">BBC Radio 1</a>'s playlist, and reached number six in the United Kingdom, where it has so far sold 302,493 copies.

<doc id="26020272" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26020272" title="Hoani Matenga">
Matenga made his starting debut for <a href="Otago%20Rugby%20Football%20Union">Otago</a> in their <a href="Ranfurly%20Shield">Ranfurly Shield</a> challenge against Canterbury on 12 September 2009. He was a part of the Highlanders' wider training squad for the 2010 <a href="Super%20Rugby">Super Rugby</a> season. In 2011 he signed with <a href="Stade%20Montois">Stade Montois</a> in France. Looking for a better salary and easier rugby Matenga signed with the <a href="Kubota%20Spears">Kubota Spears</a> in the <a href="Top%20League">Top League</a> in <a href="Japan%20Rugby%20Football%20Union">Japan</a> for the 2012-13 season.

<doc id="26020539" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26020539" title="Fire Plug Stakes">
The Fire Plug Stakes is an <a href="United%20States">American</a> <a href="Thoroughbred">Thoroughbred</a> <a href="horse%20race">horse race</a> held in January at <a href="Laurel%20Park%20Racecourse">Laurel Park Racecourse</a> in <a href="Laurel%2C%20Maryland">Laurel, Maryland</a>. It is open to horses four-year-olds and up and is run at six furlongs on the dirt.

<doc id="26021495" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26021495" title="2010 Canadian Direct Insurance BC Men's Curling Championship">
2010 Canadian Direct Insurance BC Men's Curling Championship
The 2010 <a href="Canadian%20Direct%20Insurance%20BC%20Men%27s%20Curling%20Championship">Canadian Direct Insurance BC Men's Curling Championship</a> (<a href="British%20Columbia">British Columbia</a>'s men's <a href="BC%20Men%27s%20Provincial%20Curling%20Championship">provincial</a> <a href="curling">curling</a> championship) was held February 1–7 at the <a href="Vernon%20Curling%20Club">Vernon Curling Club</a> in <a href="Vernon%2C%20British%20Columbia">Vernon, British Columbia</a>. The winning team will represent British Columbia at the <a href="2010%20Tim%20Hortons%20Brier">2010 Tim Hortons Brier</a> in <a href="Halifax%20Regional%20Municipality">Halifax, Nova Scotia</a>.
The teams that advanced to compete in the championships competed in either a coastal or interior championships, as part of the British Columbia Men's Curling Championship. These competitions hosted 16 regionally qualified teams in the hopes that they would make it into the Canadian Direct Insurance BC Men's Curling Championship. Only 4 berths advance to the next competition.

<doc id="26021794" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26021794" title="Robert Rumfeldt">
Robert "Rob" Rumfeldt (born February 18, 1966 in <a href="Windsor%2C%20Ontario">Windsor, Ontario</a>) is a <a href="Canada">Canadian</a> <a href="curling">curler</a> from <a href="Guelph%2C%20Ontario">Guelph, Ontario</a>. Rumfeldt was a member of the 1996 <a href="The%20Dominion%20Tankard">Ontario provincial championship</a> team, when he played second for <a href="Bob%20Ingram">Bob Ingram</a>. <a href="2013%20The%20Dominion%20Tankard">As of 2013</a>, Rumfeldt has played in eight provincial championships.
Rumfeldt won the provincial championship in 1996, playing second for Bob Ingram's <a href="Ridgetown%2C%20Ontario">Ridgetown</a> Curling Club rink which also consisted of <a href="Larry%20Smyth">Larry Smyth</a> (third) and <a href="James%20Brackett">James Brackett</a> (lead). It was Rumfeldt's only provincial title out of seven provincial championship appearances (<a href="2010%20Ontario%20Men%27s%20Curling%20Championship">as of 2010</a>). The team finished with a record of 4-7, in 10th place, one of the worst records ever for Ontario. Rumfeldt played a respectable 80%, third among seconds.

<doc id="26022529" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26022529" title="Mount Rose (New Jersey)">
Mount Rose is a narrow section of the <a href="Rocky%20Hill%20Ridge">Rocky Hill Ridge</a> in <a href="Hopewell%20Township%2C%20Mercer%20County%2C%20New%20Jersey">Hopewell Township</a>, <a href="New%20Jersey">New Jersey</a> which is 420 feet above sea level. The ridge's western end is at <a href="The%20Sourlands">The Sourlands</a> at Hopewell-Pennington Road and its eastern end is near Province Line Road. The ridge is a diabase intrusion and unlike many of the ridges in the state, it runs from northwest to southeast. Crusher Road travels along the ridge. Pennington-Rocky Hill Road, Cherry Valley Road, Hopewell-Princeton Road and Carter Road meet at a low point along the ridge at the village of <a href="Mount%20Rose%2C%20Hopewell%2C%20New%20Jersey">Mount Rose</a>.

<doc id="26023072" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26023072" title="Rocky Hill Ridge">
Rocky Hill Ridge, also known as the Mount Lucas-Rocky Hill Ridge, named after Lucas Voorhees, an 18th-century landowner, is a <a href="diabase">diabase</a> <a href="trap%20rock">trap rock</a> <a href="ridge">ridge</a> running west to east in the <a href="U.S.%20State">U.S. State</a> of <a href="New%20Jersey">New Jersey</a>. Diabase intrusions form Baldpate Mountain and Pennington Mountain, the <a href="Mount%20Rose%20%28New%20Jersey%29">Mount Rose</a> extension of the Mount Lucas-Rocky Hill ridge, and part of the <a href="Sourland%20Mountain">Sourland Mountains</a>. The Ridge is nine miles long and continues across the <a href="Millstone%20River">Millstone River</a>, just below <a href="County%20Route%20518%20%28New%20Jersey%29">The Georgetown Franklin Turnpike</a>, as the Ten-Mile Run Mountain and Lawrence Brook Mountain. The western section of the ridge, which runs to the northwest to <a href="The%20Sourlands">The Sourlands</a> (although not connecting with it because of the Hopewell Fault) is the <a href="Mount%20Rose%20%28New%20Jersey%29">Mount Rose</a> section of the ridge.

Kristiyan Koev spent his childhood in Havana, Cuba. His stepfather was Manuel Duchesne Cuzán <a href="http%3A//www.encaribe.org/es/article/manuel-duchesne-cuzan/320"></a> – professor at Alejandro García Caturla Conservatoire, General Director of the National Symphonic Orchestra of Cuba, Chief of the Musical Department of Symphonic Music from the Management Music at the Ministry of Culture, also head of the staff of Orchestral Direction at the Superior Institute of Art (ISA).

<doc id="26025115" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26025115" title="Italian Senate election in Lombardy, 2006">
<doc id="26025136" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26025136" title="R. Paramashivan">
<doc id="26025139" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26025139" title="CJK Unified Ideographs Extension A">
<doc id="26025178" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26025178" title="Command Loss Timer Reset">
<doc id="26025187" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26025187" title="Forrest's Cavalry Corps">
After the campaign ended, Forrest regrouped his corps in northern Mississippi, where he attempted to replenish his equipment and recruit additional men, even offering a twenty-day furlough to any man who brought in a new recruit. In January, Richard Taylor named Forrest commander of all cavalry units in the <a href="Department%20of%20Alabama%2C%20Mississippi%2C%20and%20East%20Louisiana">Department of Alabama, Mississippi, and East Louisiana</a>; Forrest reorganized his forces into four divisions split along state lines, commanded by Chalmers, Buford, Jackson, and Tyree Bell. Union diversions staged throughout the early months of 1865 forced Forrest to disperse his men across a wide region. In late March, Union Major General <a href="James%20H.%20Wilson">James H. Wilson</a> started a massive raid through Alabama, with the intention of destroying Confederate industrial centers, especially the factories located at <a href="Selma%2C%20Alabama">Selma, Alabama</a>. Forrest attempted to delay Wilson near Plantersville on April 1 in order to gain time for his scattered force to concentrate but Wilson overran the Confederate positions, taking 300 prisoners and forcing Forrest to retreat into the defenses of Selma. Once in Selma, Forrest attempted to gather every man capable of fighting, including the local home guard and militia, into the city's defenses works but he had too few troops to adequately man the works. Wilson launched an attack in the late afternoon of April 2 and quickly overran the defenses, capturing 2,700 men and thirty cannons while losing only 350 men himself. Over the next few weeks, Forrest attempted to gather and reorganize his corps; when he received word that Taylor had surrendered his department, Forrest formally surrendered his command on May 9.

<doc id="26026527" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26026527" title="2011 United States federal budget">
It was widely anticipated that a <a href="Government%20shutdown%23Potential%20government%20shutdown%20of%202011">government shutdown on April 8, 2011</a> was possible if a budget resolution or a seventh continuing resolution was not passed by the expiration of the sixth continuing resolution on April 8, 2011, which would have caused the <a href="furlough">furlough</a> of 800,000 out of 2 million civilian federal employees. However, a deal was reached with just hours remaining before the deadline, averting the shutdown. The deal included $38.5 billion in cuts from what had been budgeted for 2010, in addition to another $10 billion in cuts that had been imposed in some of the continuing resolutions. However, the April 13 Congressional Budget Office estimate showed that, compared with then-current spending rates, the spending bill would cut federal outlays from non-war accounts by just $352 million through Sept. 30. About $8 billion in immediate cuts to domestic programs and foreign aid were offset by nearly equal increases in defense spending.

<doc id="26026872" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26026872" title="Jimmy Cochran">
Born in <a href="Burlington%2C%20Vermont">Burlington, Vermont</a>, Cochran is the son of <a href="Bob%20Cochran%20%28skier%29">Bob Cochran</a>, one of the "<a href="Skiing%20Cochrans">Skiing Cochrans</a>" family of <a href="Richmond%2C%20Vermont">Richmond, Vermont</a>. He represented the U.S. in the <a href="Alpine%20skiing%20at%20the%20Winter%20Olympics">Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="Alpine%20skiing%20at%20the%202006%20Winter%20Olympics">2006</a> and <a href="Alpine%20skiing%20at%20the%202010%20Winter%20Olympics">2010</a> and the <a href="FIS%20Alpine%20World%20Ski%20Championships">World Championships</a> in <a href="FIS%20Alpine%20World%20Ski%20Championships%202005">2005</a>, <a href="FIS%20Alpine%20World%20Ski%20Championships%202007">2007</a>, and <a href="FIS%20Alpine%20World%20Ski%20Championships%202009">2009</a>.
Cochran retired from international competition after the <a href="2012%20Alpine%20Skiing%20World%20Cup">2012 season</a> and became an assistant alpine ski coach at the <a href="University%20of%20Vermont">University of Vermont</a> in Burlington. He raced for the <a href="Vermont%20Catamounts">Catamounts</a> in 2003, after transferring from <a href="Middlebury%20College">Middlebury College</a>, then was named to the <a href="United%20States%20Ski%20Team">U.S. Ski Team</a>.

<doc id="26027181" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26027181" title="Supermarine Spitfire">
Well-known Spitfire pilots included <a href="Johnnie%20Johnson%20%28RAF%20officer%29">"Johnnie" Johnson</a> (34 enemy aircraft shot down), who flew the Spitfire right through his operational career from late 1940 to 1945. <a href="Douglas%20Bader">Douglas Bader</a> (20 e/a) and <a href="Robert%20Stanford%20Tuck">"Bob" Tuck</a> (27 e/a) flew Spitfires and Hurricanes during the major air battles of 1940, and both were shot down and became <a href="Prisoners-of-war">prisoners of war</a> while flying Spitfires over France in 1941 and 1942. <a href="Paddy%20Finucane">Paddy Finucane</a> (28–32 e/a) scored all his successes in the fighter before disappearing over the <a href="English%20Channel">English Channel</a> in July 1942. Some notable Commonwealth pilots were <a href="George%20Beurling">George Beurling</a> (31 e/a) from Canada, <a href="Adolph%20Malan">"Sailor" Malan</a> (27 e/a) from South Africa, New Zealanders <a href="Alan%20Christopher%20Deere">Alan Deere</a> (17 e/a) and <a href="Colin%20Falkland%20Gray">C F Gray</a> (27 e/a) and the Australian Hugo Armstrong (12 e/a).

He also built much of the Canadian Army camp in Newmarket during WWII. The camp was pulled down at war's end but the PMQs (married quarters),drill hall and the officers mess still stand. The PMQs are private homes on Arthur St. and surrounding streets,the drill hall is the Newmarket Curling Club and the officers mess is the Royal Canadian Legion on Srigley St. 'Jack' had a construction company in Aurora called ABC,Aurora Building Corp. which he ran until his death in 1956.

<doc id="26028373" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26028373" title="Lady Godiva in popular culture">
The wooden effigy of "<a href="Peeping%20Tom">Peeping Tom</a>" which, from 1812 until <a href="World%20War%20II">World War II</a> looked out on the world from a hotel at the northwest corner of Hertford Street, Coventry, can now be found in Cathedral Lanes Shopping Centre. It represents a man in armour and was probably an image of <a href="Saint%20George">Saint George</a>. Nearby, in the 1950s rebuilt Broadgate, an animated "Peeping Tom" watches over Lady Godiva as she makes her hourly ride around the "Godiva Clock".

<doc id="26028528" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26028528" title="Formosa (surname)">
<doc id="26028535" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26028535" title="Malmesbury Branch Line">
Accordingly, the line was ceremonially opened amongst great celebration on 17 December 1877, and to ordinary public operation the following day. There were six mixed (passenger and goods) trains each way, Monday to Saturday. It was a single track of standard gauge, using Vignoles (flat-bottom) rails. The "one engine in steam" system of operation was to be used and there was one intermediate station at Somerford (later "Great Somerford"), which did not have goods facilities at first. The junction with the GWR main line was at Dauntsey, between Swindon and Chippenham, where branch trains had a bay platform. Branch trains did not run beyond Dauntsey; there was a short length of loop siding alongside the branch line at Dauntsey, used for running round passenger trains. The line was 6 miles 4 furlongs and 1½ chains (10.5 km) in length; there was a tunnel at Malmesbury, and the station there was on Gloucester Road just beyond Stanes river bridge. The construction had cost £76,565 so far—the final cost was to be £87,094.
After the War, passenger usage of the line declined abruptly; a two-hourly regular bus service from Swindon to Bristol via Malmesbury was started in 1948, providing much more convenience than the train service, and other services to Chippenham and elsewhere soon followed. A survey showed that only 23 passengers used the 11:35 train from Malmesbury in a sample week. Closure was inevitable despite local opposition, and the last train ran on 8 September 1951.

<doc id="26028916" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26028916" title="Gravity (Pixie Lott song)">
The <a href="music%20video">music video</a> for the song, directed by Nick Frew, was shot in January 2010 and premiered on 6 February 2010 on <a href="Channel%204">Channel 4</a> in the UK. It features Lott and two backup dancers performing a <a href="contemporary%20dance">contemporary routine</a> in black <a href="ballet%20tutu">tutus</a>, Lott standing on a platform in a <a href="burlesque">burlesque</a>-inspired outfit (with a black-feathered dress, thigh high boots and brunette bob, with a red circle behind her) and also performing an <a href="aerial%20silk">aerial silk</a> routine in a red catsuit. Lott is also seen singing while lying down against a mirrored surface, giving the impression she is floating in air.

<doc id="26029112" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26029112" title="West Central High School">
West Central High School, or WCHS, is a <a href="Public%20school%20%28government%20funded%29">public</a> four-year <a href="high%20school">high school</a> located near <a href="Biggsville%2C%20Illinois">Biggsville, Illinois</a>, a <a href="village">village</a> in <a href="Henderson%20County%2C%20Illinois">Henderson County, Illinois</a>, in the <a href="Midwestern%20United%20States">Midwestern United States</a>. WCHS is part of <a href="West%20Central%20Community%20Unit%20School%20District%20235">West Central Community Unit School District 235</a>, which serves the communities of <a href="Oquawka%2C%20Illinois">Oquawka</a>, <a href="Gladstone%2C%20Illinois">Gladstone</a>, <a href="Biggsville%2C%20Illinois">Biggsville</a>, <a href="Gulf%20Port%2C%20Illinois">Gulf Port</a>, <a href="Stronghurst%2C%20Illinois">Stronghurst</a>, <a href="Media%2C%20Illinois">Media</a>, <a href="Raritan%2C%20Illinois">Raritan</a>, <a href="Smithshire%2C%20Illinois">Smithshire</a>, and <a href="Carman%2C%20Illinois">Carman</a>, and also includes West Central Middle School, West Central Elementary School, and West Central Early Childhood Education Center The campus is two miles west of Biggsville at the intersection of US 94 and US 34, 15 miles northeast of <a href="Burlington%2C%20Iowa">Burlington, Iowa</a>, as well as 15 miles south west of <a href="Monmouth%2C%20Illinois">Monmouth, Illinois</a>, and serves a mixed <a href="village">village</a> and <a href="rural">rural</a> residential community. The school lies within the <a href="Burlington%2C%20Iowa">Burlington</a> <a href="micropolitan%20statistical%20area">micropolitan statistical area</a>. West Central High School was formed by the conolidation of Union High School and Southern High School in 2005.

<doc id="26029114" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26029114" title="Li Hongchen">
Li Hongchen (; born October 29, 1975 in <a href="Mudanjiang">Mudanjiang</a>, <a href="Heilongjiang">Heilongjiang</a>) is an internationally elite <a href="Curling">curler</a> who trains out of <a href="Harbin">Harbin</a>, <a href="People%27s%20Republic%20of%20China">China</a>.
He was added to the Chinese national team at the beginning of the 2009/2010 season. Some sources list him as the Lead for the team; however, the official release from the <a href="World%20Curling%20Federation">World Curling Federation</a> lists him as the Alternate for the <a href="China%20at%20the%202010%20Winter%20Olympics">Chinese Olympic Team</a>.
<a href="Curling%20at%20the%202010%20Winter%20Olympics">2010 Vancouver Olympic Games</a>

<doc id="26029295" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26029295" title="Zang Jialiang">
Zang Jialiang (; born January 12, 1988 in <a href="Harbin">Harbin</a>, <a href="Heilongjiang">Heilongjiang</a>) is a Chinese <a href="Curling">curler</a> who trains in <a href="Harbin">Harbin</a>.
He made his <a href="Curling%20World%20Championships">world championship</a> debut at the <a href="2008%20World%20Men%27s%20Curling%20Championship">2008 Grand Forks World Championships</a>. Team China achieved their best result to date. In the round robin portion they achieved upset wins over <a href="Kevin%20Martin%20%28curler%29">Team Canada</a> and <a href="Thomas%20Ulsrud">Team Norway</a>. They would finish in third after the round robin and for the first time a men's team from the Pacific region would qualify for the Playoffs. In the <a href="Page%20playoff%20system">3 vs. 4 Playoff match</a>, they lost to Team Norway, and again in the Bronze Medal Match.
Team China was less successful at the <a href="2009%20Ford%20World%20Men%27s%20Curling%20Championship">2009 Moncton World Championships</a>, where it placed ninth overall.

<doc id="26029800" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26029800" title="Human Target (1992 TV series)">
<a href="Ken%20Tucker">Ken Tucker</a> of "<a href="Entertainment%20Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a>" graded the series a "C−", describing the plot of the aired pilot episode as "paper-thin" and that the series as a whole "seems campy in a dumb way, with stilted dialogue and stiff action scenes". Writing in the "<a href="Chicago%20Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a>", <a href="Rick%20Kogan">Rick Kogan</a> called the series "one of the goofiest action-adventure shows you'll ever see". Terry Kelleher's review in "<a href="Newsday">Newsday</a>" complained that "the strangest aspect is that the actor playing [Chance]'s client [...] winds up grabbing more screen time than [series star Rick] Springfield". Syndicated columnist Jon Burlingame of <a href="United%20Features">United Features</a> credited the show with "some interesting effects" but called the drama itself "pretty tired", lamenting that "the outrageously appropriate comic-book style of "The Flash"" was "completely absent". Lon Grahnke of the "<a href="Chicago%20Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a>" found "part-time pop singer and [...] matinee idol" Springfield "hard to believe in the title role" as a retired Special Forces commando. (In real life, Springfield did spend time in Vietnam during the war, but as part of an Australian band entertaining American troops in 1969.)

<doc id="26031333" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26031333" title="Padborg Station">
The extensive station building has no booking office (self-service ticket machines available) but has a waiting room and toilet facilities. Office space in the station building is used by a number of railfreight companies as Padborg retains extensive railway marshalling yards north of the passenger station. A two-hourly cross-boundary Copenhagen/Flensburg service is operated by DSB and calls here, supplemented by a limited service of EuroCity trains penetrating further into Germany and an overnight sleeper service to/from Munich.

<doc id="26031943" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26031943" title="Thurlow Park (ward)">
Thurlow Park (ward)
Thurlow Park ward is an administrative division of the <a href="London%20Borough%20of%20Lambeth">London Borough of Lambeth</a>, England.
At the <a href="Lambeth%20Council%20election%2C%202010">Lambeth Council elections, 2010</a> residents of Thurlow Park ward elected two <a href="Conservative%20Party%20%28UK%29">Conservative Party</a> Councillors and one <a href="Labour%20Party%20%28UK%29">Labour Party</a> Councillor. 
At the <a href="Lambeth%20Council%20election%2C%202014">Lambeth Council elections, 2014</a> residents of Thurlow Park ward elected three <a href="Labour%20Party%20%28UK%29">Labour Party</a> Councillors.

<doc id="26032370" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26032370" title="Bally Haly Golf &amp; Curling Club">
Bally Haly Golf &amp; Curling Club
Bally Haly Golf & Curling Club ( ), is a semi-private <a href="curling">curling</a> club and <a href="golf%20course">golf course</a> located in <a href="St.%20John%27s%2C%20Newfoundland%20and%20Labrador">St. John's</a>, <a href="Newfoundland%20and%20Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, <a href="Canada">Canada</a>. It is the oldest golf club in <a href="Atlantic%20Canada">Atlantic Canada</a>, having been founded in 1896. In that year, a group of ten prominent Newfoundland gentlemen formed the Newfoundland Golf Club.

<doc id="26035749" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26035749" title="Richard Bentley (publisher)">
On 3 June 1829, Bentley signed a partnership agreement with <a href="Henry%20Colburn">Henry Colburn</a>. Colburn was in financial trouble and owed the Bentleys money. Rather than see him default, the two firms agreed to merge, with the agreement favouring Colburn. Over the course of a trial three-year period, Bentley was obliged to invest £2,500, find new manuscripts to publish, and act as bookkeeper. He would, in return, receive two-fifths of the profits. Colburn, on the other hand, provided three-fifths of the capital and received three-fifths of the profits. The two would make publishing decisions together. If the partnership failed before three years had passed, Bentley would be obliged to buy out Colburn for £10,000, with Colburn agreeing to publish only what he had published before the agreement. The new firm, Henry Colburn and Richard Bentley, which lasted a little over three years, was located at 8 New Burlington Street.
By 1831, the partnership between Bentley and Colburn was fraying. The cost of buying copyrights was mounting and the firm was in financial chaos. By early 1832, Bentley and Colburn were no longer speaking to each other and their dispute had to be mediated by lawyers and clerks. On 1 September 1832, Bentley and Colburn signed a settlement in which Bentley agreed to buy the firm for £1,500, keep the office on New Burlington Street, and rename the business "Richard Bentley". He paid Colburn £5,580 for materials and copyrights owned by the firm, including the Standard Novels series. Colburn agreed to a series of restrictions on his publications, an agreement which he violated almost immediately. The partnership was officially dissolved with effect from 31 August 1832.

<doc id="26036105" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26036105" title="Corinbank Festival">
Between 2008 and 2010 the festival was held on the last weekend of February. However, due to record rainfall flooding the festival site the night before the 2012 festival, it had to be postponed until the first weekend in December. The festival takes place over 3 days with music, theatre, art, burlesque, creative campsites, hiking and other family friendly activities and workshops.
Amax, Beth n Ben, Big Score, The Brass Knuckle Brass Band, The Burley Griffin, Busby Marou, Caity Sarah, Cilla Jane, Cracked Actor, D'Opus & Roshambo, Dallas Frasca, Drew Walky and the Hypnotic Planigales, Fun Machine, Hashemoto, Heath CUllen, Jack Carty, James Fahy and his Trio, Julia and the Deep Sea Sirens, Los Chavos, Lucie Thorne, Matt Dent, Moochers Inc, No Hausfrau, Pocket Fox, Son of Rut, The Barons of Tang, The Ellis Collective, The Fuelers, Waterford, ZoOpaGOo.
<doc id="26036115" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26036115" title="Liu Xian">
<doc id="26036119" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26036119" title="Exchequer of Chester">
<doc id="26036125" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26036125" title="Robert Roberts (footballer, born 1864)">
Described as "a good athlete and a useful boxer", Roberts had a "burly frame" and soon became an established member of the Wanderers' eleven. Roberts scored on his debut, in a friendly match against <a href="Preston%20North%20End%20F.C.">Preston North End</a> and was soon converted to a wing-half. In <a href="1887%E2%80%9388%20FA%20Cup">1887</a>, Bolton Wanderers were involved in a protracted first round F.A. Cup match against <a href="Everton%20F.C.">Everton</a>. Roberts scored the only goal of the initial match played on 15 October 1887, but the result was declared invalid as Bolton had fielded an ineligible player, Robert Struthers. There then followed two drawn matches (with Roberts again scoring in the first), before Everton won the second replay (the fourth match altogether) 2–1. This time, however, Everton were disqualified for fielding two professional players who had been registered as amateurs, and the match was awarded to Bolton, who were then defeated 9–1 by Preston North End, with <a href="Jimmy%20Ross%20%28footballer%20born%201866%29">Jimmy Ross</a> scoring six goals.

<doc id="26038653" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26038653" title="The Virtual Revolution">
The programme team interviewed a number of people who have played a part in the development of the web, including its inventor <a href="Tim%20Berners-Lee">Sir Tim Berners-Lee</a> and founders of notable brands; <a href="Bill%20Gates">Bill Gates</a> (<a href="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>), <a href="Steve%20Wozniak">Steve Wozniak</a> (<a href="Apple%20Inc.">Apple</a>), <a href="Chad%20Hurley">Chad Hurley</a> (<a href="YouTube">YouTube</a>), <a href="Jimmy%20Wales">Jimmy Wales</a> (<a href="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>), <a href="Stewart%20Brand">Stewart Brand</a> (<a href="The%20WELL">The WELL</a>), <a href="Biz%20Stone">Biz Stone</a> and <a href="Evan%20Williams%20%28Internet%20entrepreneur%29">Evan Williams</a> (<a href="Twitter">Twitter</a>), <a href="Peter%20Thiel">Peter Thiel</a> (<a href="PayPal">PayPal</a>) and <a href="Martha%20Lane%20Fox">Martha Lane Fox</a> (<a href="lastminute.com">lastminute.com</a>). Academics, including <a href="Terry%20Winograd">Terry Winograd</a>, <a href="Sherry%20Turkle">Sherry Turkle</a>, <a href="A.%20C.%20Grayling">A. C. Grayling</a>, <a href="David%20Runciman">David Runciman</a>, <a href="Ross%20J.%20Anderson%20%28professor%29">Ross Anderson</a> and <a href="Nigel%20Shadbolt">Nigel Shadbolt</a>, commentators, including <a href="David%20Weinberger">David Weinberger</a>, <a href="Lee%20Siegel%20%28cultural%20critic%29">Lee Siegel</a>, <a href="Douglas%20Rushkoff">Douglas Rushkoff</a>, <a href="Andrew%20Keen">Andrew Keen</a> and <a href="Stephen%20Fry">Stephen Fry</a>, and <a href="President%20of%20Estonia">Estonian President</a> <a href="Toomas%20Hendrik%20Ilves">Toomas Ilves</a> were also interviewed. Footage of the interviews was also made available on the programme's website.

<doc id="26040324" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26040324" title="BioTek">
The firm's marketing effort is led by Peter Weith, and Briar Alpert's brother Adam is the vice president of business development. BioTek's first website appeared in 1996, and has since been updated and expanded to offer multi-lingual access. In 2007 it launched an online customer resource center and opened offices in <a href="China">China</a>, <a href="India">India</a>, and <a href="Singapore">Singapore</a>. In 2008 it held a global sales meeting in <a href="Burlington%2C%20Vermont">Burlington, Vermont</a> which was attended by worldwide staff and distributors from 42 countries. It has distributors in nations such as <a href="New%20Zealand">New Zealand</a>. Additional expansions were seen in 2009 and 2010 with a corporate headquarters expansion and the opening of a Swiss office, respectively.

<doc id="26042075" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26042075" title="Bandra Terminus railway station">
Bandra Terminus is a railway terminus in <a href="Bandra">Bandra</a> (E) from where trains bound for northern and western <a href="India">India</a> are scheduled regularly. It is one of the six railway terminus within Mumbai City. The other five terminus are - <a href="Mumbai%20CST">Mumbai CST</a>, <a href="Mumbai%20Central%20railway%20station">Mumbai Central</a>, <a href="Lokmanya%20Tilak%20Terminus">Lokmanya Tilak Terminus</a> (Kurla Terminus) and <a href="Dadar%20railway%20station">Dadar</a>(Central Railway) & <a href="Dadar%20railway%20station">Dadar</a> (Western Railway). It was built in the 1990s to decongest the main <a href="Mumbai%20Central%20railway%20station">Mumbai Central</a> station. Presently about 49 trains use this station.
Bandra Terminus is close to 'Bandra-Kurla Complex', a commercially important part of Mumbai as well as Mumbai Airport.
<doc id="26042084" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26042084" title="Subrebinea">
<doc id="26042096" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26042096" title="Subterinebrica">
<doc id="26042098" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26042098" title="Minute to Win It">
<doc id="26042106" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26042106" title="Allchurch">
<doc id="26042120" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26042120" title="Battle of First Bar">
During the land operations, Lieutenant Watson of the "Calliope" and other officers boarded the "Cambridge", and soon captured it after a resistance from the few Chinese crew that remained. The ship was found mounting 34 guns. Orders were sent to the officer to set it on fire. Shortly after dark, the fire exploded its <a href="Magazine%20%28artillery%29">magazine</a>, hurling the <a href="Mast%20%28naval%29">masts</a> and <a href="Beam%20%28nautical%29">beams</a> in the air. Herbert wrote that the explosion was so loud that it "must have been heard at Canton." A total of 98 Chinese guns were captured during the day. The British casualties were one seaman killed, six seamen wounded, and two marines wounded. The seaman who died on the "Modeste" had the hammer of his <a href="musket">musket</a> caught on the ship's <a href="thwart">thwart</a> and when the piece discharged, the ball shot through his head.

<doc id="26042955" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26042955" title="2010 Newfoundland and Labrador Tankard">
The 2010 Newfoundland and Labrador Tankard will be the 2010 edition of the <a href="Newfoundland%20and%20Labrador%20Provincial%20Men%27s%20Curling%20Championship">Newfoundland and Labrador Provincial Men's Curling Championship</a>. It was held February 2–7 at the <a href="Bally%20Haly%20Golf%20%26amp%3B%20Curling%20Club">Bally Haly Golf & Curling Club</a> in <a href="St.%20John%27s%2C%20Newfoundland%20and%20Labrador">St. John's, Newfoundland and Labrador</a>.

<doc id="26044162" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26044162" title="Cystolepiota bucknallii">
The <a href="Spore%20print">spore mass</a> is white. With the aid of a light microscope, the <a href="basidiospore">spores</a> are seen ellipsoid, smooth and colourless. When <a href="Melzer%27s%20reagent">Melzer's reagent</a> is applied, the spore walls barely stain; hence, the spores are weakly <a href="Amyloid%20%28mycology%29">dextrinoid</a>. Their dimensions are 7.5–10 <a href="micrometre">µm</a> by 1–3.5 µm.

<doc id="26046103" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26046103" title="Óláfr Leggsson">
Olafr is believed to have been the son of the Icelandic priest Leggr Torfason. He is mentioned in "Sturlunga Saga" as being involved with the killing of Snorri Sturluson's only legitimate son, Jon Murti. Very little of Olafr Leggson's poetry survives, but he is credited in Skaldatal as being King <a href="Haakon%20IV%20of%20Norway">Hakon Hakonarson</a>'s court poet.

The story of Tamerlane has a long legacy associated with <a href="Orientalism">Orientalism</a> in Europe, with such publications as "Tamburlaine the Great" by <a href="Christopher%20Marlowe">Christopher Marlowe</a> in 1590, or <a href="Handel">Handel</a>'s opera "Tamerlano" in 1724.

<doc id="26050185" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26050185" title="Beurlenia">
Beurlenia
Beurlenia araripensis is an extinct species of <a href="Caridea">shrimp</a> in its own <a href="genus">genus</a>, Beurlenia. It is named after the German palaeontologist <a href="Karl%20Beurlen">Karl Beurlen</a> (1901–1985).

<doc id="26050804" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26050804" title="Aglaogonia">
<doc id="26050813" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26050813" title="Danny Andrew">
He extended his contract in December 2013 at Moss Rose until the end of the <a href="2013%E2%80%9314%20Football%20Conference">2013–14</a> season. On 26 December 2013, Andrew scored the second goal on 29 minutes in the 3–0 win over <a href="Hyde%20United%20F.C.">Hyde</a>; a free-kick, which curled low around the wall and into the bottom left corner for his second goal in four games. Two days later he scored the decisive goal 7 minutes from time in the 3–2 away victory at <a href="Grimsby%20Town%20F.C.">Grimsby</a>; a free-kick, which curled into the top right corner which gave the goalkeeper <a href="James%20McKeown">McKeown</a> no chance. On 14 February 2014, Andrew scored a 38th-minute equaliser in the 2–1 home defeat to <a href="Luton%20Town%20F.C.">Luton Town</a>; moving into the centre of the field, he let fly from 20 yards with a left footed shot from outside the box into the bottom right corner.

<doc id="26054207" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26054207" title="1948 Army Cadets football team">
<doc id="26054228" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26054228" title="Winchester City Council election, 2008">
<doc id="26054262" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26054262" title="Muzika Poludelih">
<doc id="26054263" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26054263" title="Mount Fryatt">
<doc id="26054264" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26054264" title="Denny Lodge">
Also found near the centre of the parish is a dyked enclosure known as Bishops Dyke, or The Bishop of Winchester's Purlieu. The earthwork comprises a bank, around 1 metre high and 4 metres wide, between ditches. The precise purpose of the enclosure is not known - it may have been used as a park for grazing, but the current quality of the grazing is poor. The local legend states that <a href="John%2C%20King%20of%20England">King John</a> and the <a href="bishop%20of%20Winchester">bishop of Winchester</a> were once riding together in the New Forest when the king laughingly told the bishop that he might have "as much land as he could crawl round." The bishop, who was rather fat, had a contraption made to help support him, and so managed to "crawl" round a large area. This became the Bishop's Purlieu.

<doc id="26056945" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26056945" title="Clooney Gaels GAC">
Clooney Gaels are a <a href="Gaelic%20Athletic%20Association">Gaelic Athletic Association</a> <a href="hurling">hurling</a> club based in Clooney (Cloney) outside <a href="Ahoghill">Ahoghill</a>, <a href="County%20Antrim">County Antrim</a>, <a href="Northern%20Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. This team's catchment area is Ahoghill, Clooney, Portglenone and Moneyglass.
"The Gaels" had a very impressive run in the Junior Hurling Championship, winning the County Antrim Junior Hurling Championship, Ulster Junior Hurling Championship and playing their way to the All-Ireland Junior Hurling Championship before being defeated by <a href="Danesfort%20GAA">Danesfort</a> (<a href="Kilkenny%20GAA">Kilkenny</a>).

<doc id="26057448" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26057448" title="Prophetstown High School">
The history of <a href="Tampico%2C%20Illinois">Tampico</a> Schools date back to 1874. Until 1912, the high school only had three grades. The brick building that housed TTHS for 75 years was built in 1921 and had 14 classrooms and a gymnasium. It was located near a railroad junction of the Hooppole, Yorktown & Tampico Railroad and the Chicago, Burlington & Quincy Railroad. The first mentioned was abandoned in 1953. In 1967, there were 153 students enrolled at TTHS. In the 1980s, Tampico lost its main railroad, the Chicago, Burlington & Quincy route, that was the reason Tampico became a settlement like most other small towns. Declining enrollment and financial concerns led to the closing of Tampico High School in 1996. The 1921 brick building was torn down during the summer of 2012 as part of a district wide facility improvement plan.. As of 2003, the old football field is still there, along with the padded hitting machine which is now rusted. The track outside of the field is still there in cement form. High School students from Tampico now attend Prophetstown High School, twelve miles to the northwest.

<doc id="26058860" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26058860" title="Fort Smith Transit">
Fort Smith Transit is the primary provider of <a href="mass%20transportation">mass transportation</a> in <a href="Sebastian%20County%2C%20Arkansas">Sebastian County, Arkansas</a>. Fix routes are operated Monday through Saturday on an hourly schedule with two timed-transfer points. One additional route operates Monday through Friday and has a timed-transfer point with one other route.

<doc id="26060149" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26060149" title="Yasuhito Sugiyama">
<doc id="26060154" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26060154" title="Joseph Sewall">
Sewall was born in <a href="Old%20Town%2C%20Maine">Old Town, Maine</a>, son of James Wingate Sewall and Louise Gray Sewall in the home that his great grandfather and <a href="Speaker%20of%20the%20Maine%20House%20of%20Representatives">Speaker of the Maine House of Representatives</a>, <a href="George%20P.%20Sewall">George P. Sewall</a>, built between 1830 and 1851. His maternal grandfather, George Gray, founded <a href="Old%20Town%20Canoe%20Co.">Old Town Canoe Co.</a> He attended local schools, <a href="Holderness%20School">Holderness School</a>, and <a href="Bowdoin%20College">Bowdoin College</a>, A.B. 1941, Doctor of Civil Law, Honoris Causa, 1983 <a href="https%3A//docs.google.com/viewer%3Furl%3Dhttps%253A%252F%252Flibrary.bowdoin.edu%252Farch%252Fcollections%252Fcollege-archives-and-records-management%252Fhonors%252Fsewal83.pdf"></a> . After graduation (accelerated) from college he enlisted in the <a href="U.S.%20Navy">U.S. Navy</a> in 1943 during <a href="World%20War%20II">World War II</a> as an aerial navigator, specializing in celestial navigation. Shortly after the end of the War, and after his father's death in 1946, he became President of <a href="James%20W.%20Sewall%20Company">James W. Sewall Company</a> in Old Town, an international consulting forestry and engineering firm. He later was elected to the Old Town City Council and then to the <a href="Maine%20State%20Senate">Maine State Senate</a> in 1967. Sewall served as <a href="List%20of%20Presidents%20of%20the%20Maine%20Senate">President of the Maine Senate</a> from 1975 to 1982. He was succeeded in the Maine Senate in 1982 by Democrat Michael Pearson. Upon leaving the legislature, Sewall was appointed to the Board of Trustees of <a href="Maine%20Maritime%20Academy">Maine Maritime Academy</a> by Governor <a href="Joseph%20Brennan">Joseph Brennan</a>. Soon after his appointment, he was elected Chairman, a post he held for 20 years. He was also appointed by President George H.W. Bush to be a U.S. Commissioner of the <a href="Roosevelt%20Campobello%20International%20Park">Roosevelt Campobello International Park</a> Joint Commission and a Member of the *<a href="http%3A//oai.dtic.mil/oai/oai%3Fverb%3DgetRecord%26amp%3BmetadataPrefix%3Dhtml%26amp%3Bidentifier%3DADA223178">Commission on Merchant Marine and Defense</a> by President <a href="Ronald%20Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> and re-appointments by President <a href="George%20H.W.%20Bush">George H.W. Bush</a>. He was a Trustee of <a href="Eastern%20Maine%20Medical%20Center">Eastern Maine Medical Center</a>, and a Director of Merchants National Bank, its successor, Merrill Merchants Bank, then its successor, <a href="People%27s%20United%20Bank">People's United Bank</a> (Bangor District), all of Bangor. Sewall was a moderate <a href="Maine%20Republican%20Party">Republican</a>.

<doc id="26060369" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26060369" title="George Scott III">
George Leonard Scott III was born in <a href="Burlington%2C%20Iowa">Burlington, Iowa</a>, on October 16, 1953. He moved to <a href="Sarasota%2C%20Florida">Sarasota, Florida</a>, while a teenager, and attended high school there. One of his classmates was <a href="Paul%20Reubens">Paul Reubens</a>, better known as <a href="Pee%20Wee%20Herman">Pee Wee Herman</a>. Scott was interested in film and stage work at this point in his life, and he was planning to pursue a career of some type in film.
George Scott was buried in his hometown of Burlington, Iowa.

<doc id="26063921" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26063921" title="John Ellicott">
<doc id="26063934" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26063934" title="List of Hurd band members">
Otgonbayar composed his first song for Hurd in 1993, a <a href="power%20ballad">power ballad</a> named "Chimeegüi irekh durlal", later released on <a href="The%20Best%20Collection%20I">The Best Collection I</a>. Being one of the most famous of Hurd's songs, it is played live at virtually every Hurd concert. To this day, Otgonbayar has written more than half of <a href="Hurd%20discography">Hurd's music</a>, with over 50 songs to his credit.

<doc id="26064082" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=26064082" title="Ziri Rideaux">
In September 1996 Rideaux moved to <a href="Los%20Angeles">Los Angeles</a>. Her company Zirius Film Productions produces hard-hitting <a href="documentaries">documentaries</a> and <a href="feature%20films">feature films</a>. Her documentary Treewoman about <a href="Julia%20Butterfly%20Hill">Julia Butterfly Hill</a> won international acclaim and various awards (among others, the prestigious <a href="International%20Documentary%20Association">International Documentary Association</a>/Pare Lorentz Award). Other documentaries like Tornadoes, Curlers Against Misery, Burning Man as well as her TV-series Cowgirls were broadcast on TV-stations all over the world. In 2001, Rideaux wrote, directed and produced Backgammon, a futuristic <a href="Arthouse">Arthouse</a> feature that won critical acclaim at festivals in <a href="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="London">London</a> and <a href="Cannes">Cannes</a>, where it received the <a href="Cannes%20Film%20Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a> Independent Award - handed to Rideaux by <a href="Albert%20II%2C%20Prince%20of%20Monaco">Albert II, Prince of Monaco</a>.
<a href="http%3A//www.imdb.com/title/tt0398909/">Curlers Against Misery </a> (2004) (TV)
